<p>The <b>University of Western Ontario</b> (<b>UWO</b>; branded as <b>Western University</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/London,_Ontario" title="London, Ontario">London, Ontario</a>, Canada. The main campus is located on 455 hectares (1,120 acres) of land, surrounded by residential neighbourhoods and the <a href="/wiki/Thames_River_(Ontario)" title="Thames River (Ontario)">Thames River</a> bisecting the campus's eastern portion. The university operates twelve academic faculties and schools.
</p><p>The university was founded on 7 March 1878 by Bishop <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Hellmuth" title="Isaac Hellmuth">Isaac Hellmuth</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Huron" title="Diocese of Huron">Anglican Diocese of Huron</a> as <b>The Western University of London, Ontario</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-UWO1878_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWO1878-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It incorporated <a href="/wiki/Huron_University_College" title="Huron University College">Huron College</a>, which had been founded in 1863. The first four faculties were Arts, Divinity, Law and Medicine. The university became <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational" title="Non-denominational">non-denominational</a> in 1908. Beginning in 1919, the university had affiliated with several denominational colleges. The university grew substantially in the <a href="/wiki/Post-war" title="Post-war">post-World War II</a> era, and a number of faculties and schools were added.
</p><p>Western is a <a href="/wiki/Co-educational" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-educational">co-educational</a> university, with more than 24,000 students, and over 306,000 living alumni worldwide. The university is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_Group_of_Canadian_Research_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="U15 Group of Canadian Research Universities">U15</a>, Canada's group of most distinguished research-intensive universities. Western's varsity teams, known as the <a href="/wiki/Western_Mustangs" title="Western Mustangs">Western Mustangs</a>, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference of <a href="/wiki/U_Sports" title="U Sports">U Sports</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The university was founded on 7 March 1878 by Bishop <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Hellmuth" title="Isaac Hellmuth">Isaac Hellmuth</a> of the Anglican <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Huron" title="Diocese of Huron">Diocese of Huron</a> as The Western University of London, Ontario,<sup id="cite_ref-UWO1878_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UWO1878-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and its first chancellor was Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/Richard_Martin_Meredith" title="Richard Martin Meredith">Richard Martin Meredith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It incorporated <a href="/wiki/Huron_College_(Ontario)" class="mw-redirect" title="Huron College (Ontario)">Huron College</a>, which had been founded in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first four faculties were Arts, Divinity, Law and Medicine (London Medical College).<sup id="cite_ref-not_stated_1889_295_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-not_stated_1889_295-12"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> There were originally only 15 students when classes began in 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although the university was incorporated in 1878, it was not until 20 June 1881 that it received the right to confer degrees in arts, divinity and medicine. In 1882, the name of the university was revised to The Western University and College of London, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-uwo.ca_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwo.ca-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first convocation of graduates was held on 27 April 1883.<sup id="cite_ref-not_stated_1889_295_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-not_stated_1889_295-12"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Initially affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-uwo.ca_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwo.ca-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the university became <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational" title="Non-denominational">non-denominational</a> in 1908.
</p><p>In 1916, the university's current site was purchased from the Kingsmill family. There are two World War I memorial plaques in University College. The first lists the 19 students and graduates of the University of Western Ontario who died; the second honours the men from Middlesex County who died.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NICMM_UOWO_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NICMM_UOWO-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> A third plaque lists those who served with the No. 10 Canadian General hospital during WWII, the unit raised and equipped by UWO.<sup id="cite_ref-NICMM_UOWO_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NICMM_UOWO-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1923, the university was renamed as The University of Western Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-Act1923_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Act1923-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first two buildings constructed by architect John Moore and Co. at the new site were the Arts Building (now University College) and the Natural Science Building (now the Physics and Astronomy Building).<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Classes on the university's present site began in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The University College tower, one of the university's most distinctive features, was named the Middlesex Memorial Tower in honour of the men from <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_Ontario" title="Middlesex County, Ontario">Middlesex County</a> who fought in World War I.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti 1924, University College is one of the earliest university buildings built on the present campus.</div></div></div></div>
<p>In the early 20th century, a number of institutions became <a href="/wiki/Affiliated_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Affiliated college">affiliated colleges</a> of Western. In 1919, <a href="/wiki/Brescia_University_College" title="Brescia University College">Brescia College</a> was established as a Roman Catholic affiliate of Western, while <a href="/wiki/Assumption_University_(Windsor,_Ontario)" title="Assumption University (Windsor, Ontario)">Assumption College</a> entered an affiliation agreement with the university.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ce_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Other institutions that became affiliated colleges of Western includes the Waterloo College of Arts in 1925, <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Seminary_(Diocese_of_London,_Ontario)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter's Seminary (Diocese of London, Ontario)">St. Peter's College</a> in 1939, and <a href="/wiki/King%27s_University_College_(University_of_Western_Ontario)" class="mw-redirect" title="King's University College (University of Western Ontario)">King's College</a> in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Waterloo College of Arts remained affiliated with Western until 1960, when the institution was reorganized into <a href="/wiki/Wilfrid_Laurier_University" title="Wilfrid Laurier University">Wilfrid Laurier University</a>; while Assumption College remained affiliated with Western until 1964, when it was reorganized into the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Windsor" title="University of Windsor">University of Windsor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ce_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-library-old.wlu.ca_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-library-old.wlu.ca-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Brescia College ceased operations and was integrated into Western's main campus in 2024, while Huron and King's remain independent affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Two World War II memorial honour rolls are hung on the Physics and Astronomy Building: the first lists the UWO students and graduates who served in the Second World War, and the second lists those who served with the No. 10 Canadian General hospital during WWII, the unit raised and equipped by UWO.<sup id="cite_ref-NICMM_UOWO_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NICMM_UOWO-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although enrolment was relatively small for many years, the university began to grow after World War II. It added a number of faculties in the post-war period, such as the Faculty of <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate school">Graduate Studies</a> in 1947, the School of Business Administration (now the <a href="/wiki/Ivey_Business_School" title="Ivey Business School">Ivey Business School</a>) in 1949,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the Faculty of Engineering Science (now the Faculty of Engineering) in 1957, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Law_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Law School">Faculty of Law</a> in 1959, <a href="/wiki/Althouse_College_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Althouse College of Education">Althouse College</a> (now the Faculty of Education) in 1965,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the Faculty of Music in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:WesternLawBldg.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/WesternLawBldg.jpg/250px-WesternLawBldg.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="186" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/WesternLawBldg.jpg/500px-WesternLawBldg.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2551" data-file-height="1901"></a><figcaption>The Law Building houses the university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>. The building was completed in 1960, shortly after the faculty was established.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2012, the university rebranded itself as "Western University" to give the school less of a regional or even national identity. "We want to be international," president Dr. <a href="/wiki/Amit_Chakma" title="Amit Chakma">Amit Chakma</a> told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></i>. The university's legal name, however, remains "The University of Western Ontario" and, as such, remains in use on transcripts and diplomas.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Campus">Campus</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><p>
The University of Western Ontario is in the city of London, Ontario, in the southwestern end of the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City%E2%80%93Windsor_Corridor" title="Quebec CityWindsor Corridor">Quebec CityWindsor Corridor</a>. Most of the campus is surrounded by residential neighbourhoods, with the <a href="/wiki/Thames_River_(Ontario)" title="Thames River (Ontario)">Thames River</a> bisecting the campus' eastern portion. <a href="/wiki/List_of_roads_in_London,_Ontario#Western_Road" title="List of roads in London, Ontario">Western Road</a> is the university's major transportation artery, travelling north to south. The central campus, which includes most of the university's student residences and teaching facilities is approximately 170.8 hectares (422 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-size_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-size-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UWO_Physics_and_Astronomy_building.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UWO_Physics_and_Astronomy_building.jpg/250px-UWO_Physics_and_Astronomy_building.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UWO_Physics_and_Astronomy_building.jpg/500px-UWO_Physics_and_Astronomy_building.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Physics_and_Astronomy_Building_(University_of_Western_Ontario)" title="Physics and Astronomy Building (University of Western Ontario)">Physics and Astronomy Building</a> is one of several buildings on campus built in a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic">Collegiate Gothic</a> architectural style.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The development of Western's present campus began in the 1920s. Many of the university's earliest buildings used <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic">Collegiate Gothic</a> designs.<sup id="cite_ref-camh_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camh-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> As the campus expanded in the late 1960s, the university abandoned Gothic designs in favour of <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modernist_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist architecture">modernist</a> architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-camh_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camh-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2000, planning for Western's central campus was re-conceptualized, with the core devoted for only academic buildings. The plan saw University College Hill as the focal point, linking the lower portion of the campus with the South Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-camh_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camh-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 2006 campus master plan called for the protection and renewed emphasis on Western's Collegiate Gothic buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-camh_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camh-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The oldest academic buildings within the central campus is <a href="/wiki/University_College_(University_of_Western_Ontario)" title="University College (University of Western Ontario)">University College</a> and the Physics and Astronomy Building, both completed in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-buiag_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buiag-27"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Amit Chakma Engineering Building is the newest academic building on campus, opening in September 2018. The Western Interdisciplinary Research Building, or WIRB, is the newest building on campus and houses state-of-the art research facilities for the study of <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a> as well as the Brain and Mind Institute, BrainsCAN, and the Rotman Institute for Philosophy.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Library_and_museums">Library and museums</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Library and museums"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:D_B_Weldon_Library_University_of_Western_Ontario_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/D_B_Weldon_Library_University_of_Western_Ontario_1.jpg/250px-D_B_Weldon_Library_University_of_Western_Ontario_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/D_B_Weldon_Library_University_of_Western_Ontario_1.jpg/500px-D_B_Weldon_Library_University_of_Western_Ontario_1.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="722"></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/D._B._Weldon_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="D. B. Weldon Library">D. B. Weldon Library</a> is one of the six branches of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Libraries" title="Western Libraries">Western Libraries</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The university's library system, <a href="/wiki/Western_Libraries" title="Western Libraries">Western Libraries</a>, operates six libraries that house more than 2.45 million books as of September&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, as well as electronic resources including e-books, serial titles, and databases.<sup id="cite_ref-CUDO_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CUDO-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Libraries a part of the system include the <a href="/wiki/Allyn_and_Betty_Taylor_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Allyn and Betty Taylor Library">Allyn and Betty Taylor Library</a>, C. B. Johnston Library, the <a href="/wiki/D._B._Weldon_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="D. B. Weldon Library">D. B. Weldon Library</a>, the Education Library, the John &amp; Dotsa Bitove Family Law Library, and the Music Library.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Allyn and Betty Taylor Library primarily services the faculties of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Engineering">Engineering</a>, Health Sciences, Science, and the <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Medicine_%26_Dentistry" class="mw-redirect" title="Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry">Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a>, while the C. B. Johnston Library primarily serves the <a href="/wiki/Ivey_Business_School" title="Ivey Business School">Ivey Business School</a>. The D. B. Weldon Library primarily services the faculties of Arts &amp; Humanities, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Information_%26_Media_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Information &amp; Media Studies">Information &amp; Media Studies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Sciences">Social Sciences</a>. The D. B. Weldon Library also houses the university's Archives and Research Collections Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Western Libraries also maintains the Shared Library Catalogue, which provides common access to the collections of Western Libraries, as well as the collections from the libraries of university colleges affiliated with the Western, including <a href="/wiki/Huron_University_College" title="Huron University College">Huron University College</a>, King's University College, and St. Peter's Seminary. Access to the Shared University Catalogue is provided to students and faculty of Western, and the affiliated university colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-SUC_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SUC-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:McIntosh_Gallery_UWO.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/McIntosh_Gallery_UWO.jpg/250px-McIntosh_Gallery_UWO.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/McIntosh_Gallery_UWO.jpg/500px-McIntosh_Gallery_UWO.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a><figcaption>McIntosh Gallery is one of two art galleries located on its campus.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Western also operates two art galleries, the Artlab Gallery, and the McIntosh Gallery. Located in the John Labatt Visual Arts Centre, the Artlab Gallery showcases approximately 14 projects per year, exploring conceptual and experimental production through a wide range of media. The Artlab Gallery also aims to assist in the research and practices of students and faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The McIntosh Gallery is a university-based, public art gallery, opened since 1942. The gallery is a presentation and dissemination centre for the university, as well as the London community, showcasing advanced practices and research in art history and contemporary visual art.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The gallery is the oldest university art gallery in the province of Ontario, initially opened as an exhibition of paintings by <a href="/wiki/War_artists" class="mw-redirect" title="War artists">war artists</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Canada" title="National Gallery of Canada">National Gallery of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> 683 works of the Gallery's collection were put on display throughout the university's main campus through the Gallery's ArtShare program in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-McIGR_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McIGR-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Western also maintains academic and administrative links with the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Ontario_Archaeology" title="Museum of Ontario Archaeology">Museum of Ontario Archaeology</a>. The Museum originally grew out of a collection of artifacts housed in various buildings throughout London, including Western's University College, and Middlesex College. Formally opened on 28 February 1978, its creation was facilitated by the university president and Western's Faculty of Social Science. Although the museum was incorporated as an independent charitable organization, without the ability to share capital, its directors continued to be appointed by the university's Board of Governors.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Housing_and_student_facilities">Housing and student facilities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Housing and student facilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sydenham_Quad.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Sydenham_Quad.JPG/250px-Sydenham_Quad.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Sydenham_Quad.JPG/500px-Sydenham_Quad.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a><figcaption>Sydenham Quad within <a href="/wiki/Medway-Sydenham_Hall" title="Medway-Sydenham Hall">Medway-Sydenham Hall</a>, one of nine student residences at the university's campus</figcaption></figure>
<p>The main campus of The University of Western Ontario offers student housing, with nine student residences housing either first-year students or upper-year students. In September 2015, 23.49 percent of the undergraduate population lived on campus, including 78.69 percent of all first-year students.<sup id="cite_ref-CUDO_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CUDO-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Each residence operates their own Residences' Council, governed by their own constitutions.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Student residence building are split between traditional-styled residences, suite-styled residences, and hybrid-style residences that incorporate elements of traditional and suite-styled residences.
</p><p>Traditional-styled residences include Delaware Hall, <a href="/wiki/Medway-Sydenham_Hall" title="Medway-Sydenham Hall">Medway-Sydenham Hall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saugeen-Maitland_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Saugeen-Maitland Hall">Saugeen-Maitland Hall</a>. Suite-styled residences include Alumni House, Elgin Hall, Essex Hall, and London Hall. Hybrid-styled residences include Perth Hall and Ontario Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Alumni House and London Hall are reserved strictly for upper-year students.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The largest residential building at the university is SaugeenMaitland Hall, which houses 1,252 first-year students.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Saugeen-Maitland_Hall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Saugeen-Maitland_Hall.jpg/250px-Saugeen-Maitland_Hall.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Saugeen-Maitland_Hall.jpg/500px-Saugeen-Maitland_Hall.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3510" data-file-height="2346"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Saugeen-Maitland_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Saugeen-Maitland Hall">Saugeen-Maitland Hall</a> is the largest student residence operated by the university.</figcaption></figure><p>The University Community Centre acts as Western's <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Student activity centre">student activity centre</a>, and is the university's centre of student governance and student directed social, cultural, entertainment and recreational activities. The University Community Centre contains the offices the University Students' Council.  The graduate student union, the Society of Graduate Students is located in the Middlesex College building.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Off-campus_facilities">Off-campus facilities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Off-campus facilities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In addition to The University of Western Ontario's central campus, the university owns several other properties throughout Southwestern Ontario. Excluding Western's central campus,
as well as the campuses of Western's affiliated university colleges, Western owns approximately 309.6 hectares (765 acres) of land. Included among these properties is a number of research facilities. Managed under Western Research Parks, the facilities are clustered into three <a href="/wiki/Science_park" title="Science park">research parks</a>. The three parks serve as a research link between academics and corporations.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> 
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:President%27s_House_UWO.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/President%27s_House_UWO.jpg/250px-President%27s_House_UWO.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/President%27s_House_UWO.jpg/500px-President%27s_House_UWO.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Gibbons_Lodge" title="Gibbons Lodge">Gibbons Lodge</a> serves as the official residence for the University President. It is one of several university-owned properties outside its main campus.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The oldest research park operated by Western is Discovery Park, adjacent to the university's main campus. The 16.2 hectares (40 acres) research park was established in 1989, with tenants ranging from national government laboratories, to large-multi-industrial research centres. Discovery Park also includes a 48-room hotel and conference centre, Windermere Manor.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Advanced Manufacturing Park is another research park established through a partnership between Western, <a href="/wiki/Fanshawe_College" title="Fanshawe College">Fanshawe College</a> and the City of London. Advanced Manufacturing Park is a 52.6 hectares (130 acres) research park, built in an area zoned for full-scale manufacturing and large-scale research.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/WindEEE_Dome" title="WindEEE Dome">WindEEE Dome</a> is among the facilities built in the Advanced Manufacturing Park. The WindEEE Dome is the world's first hexagonal <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnel</a>, allowing for scientists to address certain challenges related to wind. The structure is able to accommodate replicas of buildings, and bridges to test for structural integrity in a variety of wind conditions. The facility is able to physically simulate high intensity wind systems, including <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornados</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Downbursts" class="mw-redirect" title="Downbursts">downbursts</a> hard to replicate in other wind tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2003, Western opened another research park known as the Sarnia-Lambton Research park, in a joint initiative with <a href="/wiki/Lambton_County" title="Lambton County">Lambton County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarnia" title="Sarnia">Sarnia</a>. The 32.4 hectares (80 acres) research park is adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Lambton_College" title="Lambton College">Lambton College</a> and is home to Canada's largest <a href="/wiki/Clean_technology" title="Clean technology">clean technology</a> <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university also manages several residences outside the central campus. The official residence of the university president, <a href="/wiki/Gibbons_Lodge" title="Gibbons Lodge">Gibbons Lodge</a>, is off-campus. Completed in 1932, the <a href="/wiki/Tudor_Revival_architecture" title="Tudor Revival architecture">Tudor Revival-styled</a> house is north of Western's central campus. It was acquired by the university in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In addition to Gibbons Lodge, the university also maintains Platt's Lane Estates, a complex of townhouses and apartments south of the university's campus. The complex was designed to accommodate upper-year, graduate, and students with families.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sustainability">Sustainability</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sustainability"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Campus sustainability at Western is managed by the President's Advisory Committee on Environment &amp; Sustainability. The committee's mandate includes incorporating sustainability into the academic programming, engaging in research across the disciplines into issues of environmental sustainability, using ecological landscaping methods and preserving green space and building and renovating facilities in accordance with energy efficiency and sustainability principles<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Along with the other members of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ontario_Universities" title="Council of Ontario Universities">Council of Ontario Universities</a>, Western had signed a pledge in 2009 known as <i>Ontario Universities Committed to a Greener World</i>, with the objective of transforming its campus into a model of environmental responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Western is also a signatory of the <a href="/wiki/Talloires_Declaration" title="Talloires Declaration">Talloires Declaration</a>, a sustainability declaration created for presidents of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The university campus received a B grade from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Administration">Administration</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The university's governance is conducted through the Board of Governors and the Senate. The Senate was the university's first governing body, created in the university's founding document, An Act to Incorporate the Western University of London, Ontario, 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Board of Governors was later established in An Act to amend the Act to incorporate the Western University of London, Ontario, 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Board is responsible for the university's management, including financial matters.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Ex officio governors of the Board include the university's chancellor, president, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_London,_Ontario" title="List of mayors of London, Ontario">mayor of London</a>, the warden of <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_County,_Ontario" title="Middlesex County, Ontario">Middlesex County</a> and the secretary of the Board of Governors. The Board also consists of 26 other governors either appointed or elected by the members of the university's community and the surrounding community, including elected representatives from the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Senate is responsible for the university's academic policies.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Senate consists of 20 <i>ex officio</i> positions in the Senate granted to the chancellor, the president, the university's vice-presidents, the senior dean of each faculty, the university librarian and the secretary of the senate. The secretary of the senate is a non-voting <i>ex officio</i> member. The Senate also consists of 46 elected members from the university's faculty, 18 members from the student population, and 9 members from the Western's affiliated colleges, including their principals. The Senate also consists of 9 other members from around the university community. In all, there are 103 members of the Senate, 102 of which may vote and 1013 official observers of the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The president and vice-chancellor acts as the university's chief executive officer, accountable to the Board of Governors and the Senate, by supervising and directing the university's academic and administrative work and its teaching and non-teaching staff.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard_(academic)" title="Alan Shepard (academic)">Alan Shepard</a> is the tenth president of the university, who began his tenure as president on 1 July 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, Shepard was the highest paid President of any Ontario university, receiving $520,000 in salary and benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The chancellor of the university acts as the honorary and symbolic head of the university. The position of chancellor is a four-year, non-renewable term.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The university's current chancellor is Kelly Meighen, who was appointed to the position on 1 July 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Affiliated_institutions">Affiliated institutions</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Affiliated institutions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The University of Western Ontario is currently affiliated with two <a href="/wiki/University_colleges" class="mw-redirect" title="University colleges">university colleges</a>.
</p><p>Huron University College was founded in 1863, originally established as Huron College, and renamed Huron University College in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-HurH_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HurH-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Huron's affiliation with Western was authorized in Western's first provincial charter, in 1878. Both Huron and Western share the same progenitor in Bishop <a href="/wiki/Issac_Hellmuth" class="mw-redirect" title="Issac Hellmuth">Issac Hellmuth</a>. Huron moved to its present location, adjacent to Western's central campus, in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-HurH_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HurH-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> King's University College was founded in 1954, as a Catholic-based liberal arts college.<sup id="cite_ref-King_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Founded as Christ the King's College, it changed its name to King's College in 1966, and King's University College in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Regardless of the university college's religious affiliation, enrolment in those institutions is not restricted based on the student's religious beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-King_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bres_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bres-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Peter%27s_Seminary.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/St._Peter%27s_Seminary.JPG/250px-St._Peter%27s_Seminary.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/St._Peter%27s_Seminary.JPG/500px-St._Peter%27s_Seminary.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Seminary_(Diocese_of_London,_Ontario)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter's Seminary (Diocese of London, Ontario)">St. Peter's Seminary</a> is an affiliated institution of Western.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In addition to the two university colleges, Western also maintains an affiliation with St. Peter's Seminary through its affiliation with King's University College.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1912, St. Peters was opened as the <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_London,_Ontario" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of London, Ontario">Roman Catholic Diocese of London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The campuses of King's University College and St. Peter's Seminary are east of <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Highway_4" title="Ontario Highway 4">Richmond Street</a> and the university's central campus.
</p><p>From 1919 until 2024, Western was also affiliated with Brescia University College, an all-women's Catholic-based university college and the last remaining <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_college" title="Women's college">women's college</a> in Canada until its dissolution.<sup id="cite_ref-bres_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bres-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Founded by the <a href="/wiki/Ursulines" title="Ursulines">Ursulines</a> in 1919, an affiliation agreement with Western was arranged shortly after its founding, with Brescia campus moving adjacent to Western's central campus in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Brescia College began integration with Western's main campus in September 2023, and ceased operations in May 2024.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Academics">Academics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Academics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Western is a publicly funded research university, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The full-time undergraduate programs comprise the majority of the school's enrolment, made up of 30,665 full-time, part-time undergraduate students and concurrent education students. The graduate student population is 5,297, including full-time students, part-time students and post-graduate medical residents.<sup id="cite_ref-ipbuwo_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipbuwo-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The university conferred 4,504 bachelor's degrees, 207 doctoral degrees, 1,427 master's degrees, and 1,180 second entry professional degrees in 20082009.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Students may apply for financial aid such as the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Student_Assistance_Program" title="Ontario Student Assistance Program">Ontario Student Assistance Program</a> and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans and Grants</a> through the federal and provincial governments. The financial aid may come in loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Resources_and_Skills_Development_Canada_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Resources_and_Skills_Development_Canada-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:SEB_Front_Tower.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/SEB_Front_Tower.jpg/250px-SEB_Front_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="254" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/SEB_Front_Tower.jpg/500px-SEB_Front_Tower.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2678" data-file-height="2723"></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Engineering_Building" title="Spencer Engineering Building">Spencer Engineering Building</a> is used by Western's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a>. The faculty is one of eleven faculties at the university.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The university is divided into 11 faculties and schools including the <a href="/wiki/Don_Wright_Faculty_of_Music" title="Don Wright Faculty of Music">Don Wright Faculty of Music</a>, the Faculty of Arts &amp; Humanities, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Education" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Education">Faculty of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a>, Faculty of Health Sciences, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Information_%26_Media_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Information &amp; Media Studies">Faculty of Information &amp; Media Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Western Ontario Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>, Faculty of Science, Faculty of Social Science, <a href="/wiki/Ivey_School_of_Business" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivey School of Business">Ivey School of Business</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Medicine_%26_Dentistry" class="mw-redirect" title="Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry">Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In September 2016, most undergraduates at Western was enrolled in the Faculty of Social Sciences, with 7,114 full-time and part-time undergraduate students in enrolled in one of their programs.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-enrolnum_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enrolnum-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the same year, the Faculty of Health Science held the highest enrolment among graduate students at Western, with 821 full-time and part-time graduate students enrolled in the faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The School Graduate and Postdoctoral Studies is the university's central administrative unit of graduate education.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, it is not considered its own faculty or academic school.
</p><p>Admission requirements at Western differ depending upon the education system where the applicant originates from, due to the lack of uniformity in marking schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In September 2012 secondary school average for full-time first-year students at Western was 89.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> For admission in the fall of 2013, there were 45,000 applications for 4,900 spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university also offers students the opportunity to earn credits while studying abroad, through student exchange programs, and internship, faculty-led international excursions, and clinical placements.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1316064257"><table class="infobox" style="width:25em; font-size:80%"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">912</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-QS_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">6</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">THE</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">910</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><i><a href="/wiki/USNWR" class="mw-redirect" title="USNWR">USNWR</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">10</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s#University_Ranking_Guide" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> Medical/Doctoral<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">11</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s#University_Ranking_Guide" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> Reputation<sup id="cite_ref-Macrep_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macrep-90"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></th><td class="infobox-data">9</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In the 2022 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> rankings, the university ranked 201300 in the world and 912 in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 2024 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the university 114th in the world and sixth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 2023 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> ranked Western 201250 in the world, and 810 in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> 202223 global university rankings, the university placed 300th in the world, and tenth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> 2023 rankings, Western placed 11th in their Medical-Doctoral university category, tied with <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Laval" title="Universit Laval">Universit Laval</a>. The university also ranked 13th in <i>Maclean</i> reputation category.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university has also placed in a number of rankings that evaluated the employment prospects of its graduates. In QS's 2022 graduate employability ranking, the university ranked 43rd in the world, and third in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_GEUR_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS_GEUR-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university is ranked among the top 1% of higher education institutions worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Research">Research</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Research"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Robartsri2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Robartsri2.jpg/250px-Robartsri2.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Robartsri2.jpg/500px-Robartsri2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="667" data-file-height="500"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Robarts_Research_Institute" title="Robarts Research Institute">Robarts Research Institute</a> is a medical research facility at Western's campus. More than 600 people conduct basic and clinical research at the facility.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Western has four primary fields of research: life sciences and the human condition, culture analysis and values, the human and physical environments, and social trends, public policy, and economic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In Research Infosource's 2018 ranking of Canadian research universities, Western was ranked 10th; with a sponsored research income (external funding) of $249.669 million in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-reinf_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinf-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2017, members of Western's faculty averaged a sponsored research income of $166,100, while graduate students averaged a sponsored research income $41,600.<sup id="cite_ref-reinf_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reinf-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The federal government is the largest source of funding providing 46% of Western's <a href="/wiki/Funding_of_science" title="Funding of science">research budget</a>, primarily through grants. Private corporations contribute 10 per cent of Western's research budget.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Western's research performance has been noted in several <a href="/wiki/Bibliometrics" title="Bibliometrics">bibliometric</a> university rankings, which uses <a href="/wiki/Citation_analysis" title="Citation analysis">citation analysis</a> to evaluate the <a href="/wiki/Impact_factor" title="Impact factor">impact</a> a university has on academic publications. In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities</a> ranked Western 197th in the world, and ninth in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> whereas the <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a> 201819 rankings placed the university 187th in the world, and ninth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Research regarding the <a href="/wiki/Human_brain" title="Human brain">human brain</a> has also become a major focus at the university. The Brain and Mind Institute focuses on research in <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a> at Western.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the Institute discovered the blind may perform <a href="/wiki/Animal_echolocation" title="Animal echolocation">echolocation</a> by using the <a href="/wiki/Visual_cortex" title="Visual cortex">visual cortex</a> of the brain.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Another 2011 study at Western suggested people who are deaf from birth may be able to reassign the area of their brain used for hearing to boost their sight.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Western also is home to the Institute for Earth and Space Exploration, the first dedicated space institute providing a planetary science degree in Canada.
</p><p>In 2014, the university unveiled plans for a 4,200-square-foot facility for research in medicine, science and technology, in the study of HIV and other complex human pathogens. <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Medicine_%26_Dentistry" class="mw-redirect" title="Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry">Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a>'s Department of Microbiology and Immunology is globally recognized, in large part due to the groundbreaking discoveries of Dr. Chil-Yong Kang, a Western researcher clinically testing a preventive HIV/AIDS vaccine.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SAV001" title="SAV001">SAV001</a>-H is the first and only preventive <a href="/wiki/HIV_vaccine" class="mw-redirect" title="HIV vaccine">HIV vaccine</a> based on a genetically modified killed whole <a href="/wiki/HIV-1" class="mw-redirect" title="HIV-1">HIV-1</a> virus. The United States <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) Phase I clinical trial was completed in August 2013<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and reported no serious adverse effects while boosting antibodies in the volunteers. The vaccine SAV001-H holds tremendous promise, having already proven to stimulate strong immune responses in preliminary toxicology tests. It is the only HIV vaccine under development in Canada, and one of only a few in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Student_life">Student life</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Student life"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<table style="text-align:center; float:right; font-size:85%; margin-left:2em; margin:10px" class="wikitable">
