<p>The two main <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">student unions</a> on administrative and policy issues is the University Students' Council for all undergraduate students and the Society of Graduate Students for graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The University Students' Council (USC) is a <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">student-led organization</a> that exists to advocate for and support the undergraduate students. The University Students <i>Commission</i> &nbsp;was created in 1930 as a coordinating body between the existing Students Administrative Assembly (SAA), a 22-member body including representatives from each class in Arts and Sciences Faculty Councils, and the Hippocratic Council. In 1947 the name was officially changed to "University Students' Council".
</p><p>Today USC is a nonprofit organization incorporated on March 29, 1965, under the Ontario Nonprofit Corporations Act.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Its membership consists of the roughly 38,000 undergraduate students enrolled at the university. Policy papers are approved by Council, and focus on evidence-based advocacy, with recommendations informed by both research and student consultation. Part of the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Undergraduate_Student_Alliance" title="Ontario Undergraduate Student Alliance">Ontario Undergraduate Student Alliance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the USC also engages in advocacy at multiple levels of government, and across the university.
</p><p>The University Students' Council recognizes more than 220 student organizations and clubs, in which more than 15,000 students are a member.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These clubs and organizations cover a wide range of interests such as academics, culture, religion, social issues, and recreation.<sup id="cite_ref-club_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-club-115"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The University Students' Council also provides additional services such as two pub/restaurants (The Spoke and The Wave), and clothing store (The Purple Store). A student run drop-in <a href="/wiki/Food_bank" title="Food bank">food bank</a> addresses increasing food insecurity among students,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Peer_support" title="Peer support">Peer Support Centre</a> provides a safe space and resource hub for students to prioritize their well-being. A USC run movie theatre named "Western Film" screened <a href="/wiki/Discount_theater" title="Discount theater">second-run movies</a> at cheap prices from the mid-1980s until closing during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The USC collects fees and provides administrative support to two campus media outlets: The Gazette, a <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> which has been in publication since 1906,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and RadioWestern, a FM radio station broadcasting to the London area.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>
There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraternities and sororities">fraternities and sororities</a> existing throughout the student community, however, in 2021 the USC voted to remove special privileges<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Fraternity" title="Fraternity">fraternities</a>. </p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:O-Week_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/O-Week_2.jpg/250px-O-Week_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/O-Week_2.jpg/500px-O-Week_2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Orientation_week" class="mw-redirect" title="Orientation week">O-week</a> at Western is a week of activities to orient and welcome new students.</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Athletics">Athletics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Athletics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Western_Mustangs" title="Western Mustangs">Western Mustangs</a></div>
<p>Athletics at Western is managed by Sports &amp; Recreation Services, a division of the Faculty of Health Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The university's varsity teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference of <a href="/wiki/U_Sports" title="U Sports">U Sports</a>. The varsity teams are known as the <a href="/wiki/Western_Mustangs" title="Western Mustangs">Western Mustangs</a>. As is mandatory for all members of U Sports, Western does not provide full-ride athletic scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university has a number of athletic facilities open to their varsity teams and their students. The Western Student Recreation Centre, opened in January 2009, is home to Western's group fitness, drop in recreation, registered massage therapy, sport psychology, drop in recreation, intramural sports and clubs. Better known as the WSRC or the Rec Centre, this facility has an 8-lane, 50-metre pool facility and several gyms.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Football_game_at_Western_University.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Football_game_at_Western_University.jpg/250px-Football_game_at_Western_University.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Football_game_at_Western_University.jpg/500px-Football_game_at_Western_University.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a><figcaption>The Western Mustangs compete in a number of sports, including <a href="/wiki/Canadian_football" title="Canadian football">Canadian football</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Western_Alumni_Stadium" title="Western Alumni Stadium">Western Alumni Stadium</a> (Formerly TD Stadium) has been the university's main stadium since it opened in 2000, with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of over 8,000 spectators. The stadium is home to the university's varsity football team, and has hosted a number of events including the <a href="/wiki/World_Lacrosse_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="World Lacrosse Championships">World Lacrosse Championships</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Games" title="Canada Games">Canada Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Thompson Recreation &amp; Athletic Centre which houses a number of athletic venues, including an ice rink, tennis facilities and a track, is home to the varsity ice hockey teams and the varsity track and field teams.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Another athletic facility at the university is Alumni Hall, which is a multipurpose venue for sports such as basketball, volleyball and other indoor events.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many Western students take part in intramural sport leagues and tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Opportunities are offered at multiple skill levels and across a variety of sports. Sports offered include traditional sports like volleyball, basketball and soccer, as well as less traditional events like dodgeball and inner tube water polo. Western also hosts secondary school football games at TD Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Western has several fight songs and school songs that may be heard at varsity games, including the official school song, "<a href="/wiki/Western_Mustang_Band#Western_Song" title="Western Mustang Band">Western</a>". Written in 1930, it is most notably played at football games and other athletic events by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Mustang_Band" title="Western Mustang Band">Western Mustang Band</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Performances">Performances</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Performances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Don_Wright_Faculty_of_Music" title="Don Wright Faculty of Music">Don Wright Faculty of Music</a> offers almost 400 performances, masterclasses and recitals each year, most of which are open to the public. The Western University Symphony Orchestra and the Western University Chamber Orchestra perform regularly. UWOpera performs a wide variety of repertoire ranging from operetta to full operatic works in the Paul Davenport Theatre (refurbished and renamed in 2009 from Talbot Theatre).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> There are other student-run drama groups that puts on shows every year.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Media">Media</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:University_Community_Centre,_UWO.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/University_Community_Centre%2C_UWO.jpg/250px-University_Community_Centre%2C_UWO.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/University_Community_Centre%2C_UWO.jpg/500px-University_Community_Centre%2C_UWO.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1552"></a><figcaption>The University Community Centre is a <a href="/wiki/Student_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Student centre">student centre</a> that houses a number of student-run organizations, including a <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a> station, and a <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a>.</figcaption></figure> 
<p>The university's student population operates a number of media outlets throughout the campus environment. The University Students' Council owns and operates the <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a> station <a href="/wiki/CHRW-FM" title="CHRW-FM">CHRW-FM</a> (94.9 FM).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first campus radio to operate at Western was in 1971, although the present day station RadioWestern, was not established until 1979, one year after the closure of the Western's first campus radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The University Students' Council previously operated a closed-circuit television station known as tvWestern.ca. The station began broadcasting in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and was discontinued by the student union in 2010 after being cut from the University Students' Council's operating budget.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Newspaper">Newspaper</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Newspaper"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><i>The Gazette</i>, sometimes called the <i>Western Gazette</i>, is a <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" class="mw-redirect" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a> which has been in publication since 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <i>The Gazette</i> has its roots as a hand-written literature newspaper called <i>In Cap And Gown</i>, which began in 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-138"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The <i>In Cap And Gown</i> was first produced in newsprint in November 1906, but changed its name to <i>The Gazette</i> in 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-138"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The <i>Gazette</i> ceased publishing in the spring of 1916 due to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War 1</a> but was revived in 1919. In 1930, seven years after Western University changed its name to the University of Western Ontario, the paper changed its name to the <i>University of Western Ontario Gazette</i>. <i>The Gazette</i> started as monthly but in its early years appeared weekly and twice weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-139"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The <i>Gazette</i> was in print four days a week from 1991 to 2015, making it the only student newspaper in Canada to be considered a daily newspaper. In 2017, the <i>Gazette</i> began printing only once a week and shifted fully online in 2020 due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>  In 2021, the <i>Gazette</i> began a gradual return to print editions, focusing on special editions and introducing bi-weekly print issues in the fall of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p><i>The Gazette</i> has spawned several other publications in its history. One was <i>Occidentalia</i>, which had its roots in special convocation issues of the <i>Gazette</i> which included pictures of the graduating class.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The paper is owned and published by the <a href="/wiki/University_Students%27_Council_(Canada)" class="mw-redirect" title="University Students' Council (Canada)">University Students' Council</a> (USC). The paper has editorial autonomy from the USC.<sup id="cite_ref-About_Us_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Us-144"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The publications committee consists of mainly professional journalists who advise the full-time staff on editorial decisions and financial management of the paper, as well as offer an intermediary between the sometimes contentious relationship between the student politicians who are reported on by the <i>Gazette</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The paper is one of the founding members of the National University Wire.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <i>Gazette</i> alumni have worked at many successful media networks including <i>The Globe and Mail, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Post" title="National Post">National Post</a>, MacLean's, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">CBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/CTV_Television_Network" title="CTV Television Network">CTV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Arabic" title="Al Jazeera Arabic">Al Jazeera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet" title="Sportsnet">Sportsnet</a></i> and <i>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-AboutUs_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AboutUs-147"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Student_life_programs">Student life programs</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Student life programs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Leadership_education">Leadership education</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Leadership education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The Leadership Education Program is designed to teach students how to become effective leaders, both individually and in teams.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Student_exchange">Student exchange</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Student exchange"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The University of Western Ontario offers a <a href="/wiki/Student_exchange_program" title="Student exchange program">student exchange program</a> to <a href="/wiki/Study_abroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Study abroad">study abroad</a> with several other partner institutions. Almost four hundred students come to Western each year as exchange students from abroad, with more students coming to Western as international undergraduate or exchange students. The Western International Exchange Program offers its students the opportunity to study at more than 85 different institutions in 25 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sexual_violence">Sexual violence</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sexual violence"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2014, Stanley Dobrowolski, a former staff psychiatrist for Western students, was convicted of sexual crimes against his patients. He pleaded guilty to 18 charges (16 of sexual assault, one for voyeurism, and one for disobeying court orders) and was sentenced to four years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Dobrowolski had been a psychiatrist at Western until 1995. The university issued an apology for Dobrowolski's actions on 16 March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university is known for its party culture, ranking seventh in Canada by <i>Maclean's</i> party school 2019 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2021, several students were alleged to have been sexually assaulted during Western's <a href="/wiki/Orientation_week" class="mw-redirect" title="Orientation week">orientation week</a>. The incidents surfaced after numerous reports of sexual assault, many facilitated by drugs, surfaced on the internet. The resulting incidents has resulted in some criticism against the university for failing to protect female students from <a href="/wiki/Rape_culture" title="Rape culture">rape culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These events took place during a period known as the "Red Zone." This is the period encompassing the first eight weeks of the university school year in which 50% of sexual-assaults take place.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the same week, a first-year Western student was killed near the university; a suspect was later charged with manslaughter in connection with the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-LondonCTV_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LondonCTV-155"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On March 2, 2022, the University Students' Council unanimously passed a motion declaring a Sexual and Gender-Based Violence crisis on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This followed nationally discussed allegations of a mass drugging and widespread sexual-assault during the 2021/2022 Orientation Week, which culminated with the arrest and expulsion of some students.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>

<p>As of November&nbsp;2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the University of Western Ontario has over 220,000 alumni residing in over 100 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Throughout Western's history, faculty, alumni, and former students have played prominent roles in many different fields and have won the Nobel Prize, <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> and other awards such as the Rhodes Scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Former faculty member <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Banting" title="Frederick Banting">Frederick Banting</a> received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> for his discovery of insulin.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alice_Munro" title="Alice Munro">Alice Munro</a>, who won the Nobel Prize in Literature in 2013, studied in the university's English department for two years under a scholarship and returned to Western in 19741975, when she held the post of writer-in-residence. She was later awarded an honorary degree.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Former faculty member from 1972 to 1996 <a href="/wiki/Peter_Howitt_(economist)" title="Peter Howitt (economist)">Peter Howitt</a>, who had received his MA in economics at the university in 1969, was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a> in 2025 for the theory of sustained growth through "creative destruction". Two graduates from Western have also travelled in space, namely <a href="/wiki/Bjarni_Tryggvason" title="Bjarni Tryggvason">Bjarni Tryggvason</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Bondar" title="Roberta Bondar">Roberta Bondar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many former students have gained local and national prominence for serving in government, such as <a href="/wiki/James_Bartleman" title="James Bartleman">James Bartleman</a>, who served as <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Ontario" title="Lieutenant Governor of Ontario">Lieutenant Governor of Ontario</a> from 2002 to 2007, and <a href="/wiki/Sheila_Copps" title="Sheila Copps">Sheila Copps</a> who served as Deputy Prime Minister of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Western's alumni also include a number of provincial premiers, including former <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">premiers of Ontario</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Robarts" title="John Robarts">John Robarts</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Peterson" title="David Peterson">David Peterson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the former <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Alberta" title="Premier of Alberta">premier of Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Getty" title="Don Getty">Don Getty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> A number of graduates have also served prominent positions on the international level. Examples include <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Stevens" title="Glenn Stevens">Glenn Stevens</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_Australia" title="Reserve Bank of Australia">Reserve Bank of Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Chan" title="Margaret Chan">Margaret Chan</a>, the Director-General of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A significant number of prominent leaders in business and economics have also studied at Western. Examples include: Stephen Poloz, Governor, Bank of Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_H._Bailey" title="Thomas H. Bailey">Thomas H. Bailey</a>, founder and former chairman of <a href="/wiki/Janus_Capital_Group" title="Janus Capital Group">Janus Capital Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Beattie" title="Geoff Beattie">Geoff Beattie</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/The_Woodbridge_Company" title="The Woodbridge Company">The Woodbridge Company</a> and chairman of <a href="/wiki/Bell_Media" title="Bell Media">CTVglobemedia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_A._Cope" title="George A. Cope">George Cope</a>, president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Bell_Canada" title="Bell Canada">Bell Canada Enterprise</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span Financial</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lee_Seng_Wee" title="Lee Seng Wee">Lee Seng Wee</a>, former chairman of <a href="/wiki/Oversea-Chinese_Banking_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Oversea-Chinese Banking Corporation">Oversea-Chinese Banking Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Galen_Weston" hospitality training institution,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Kevin_O%27Leary" title="Kevin O'Leary">Kevin O'Leary</a>, television personality, venture capitalist, and former president of <a href="/wiki/The_Learning_Company" title="The Learning Company">The Learning Company</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Michael Katchen, co-founder, and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Wealthsimple" title="Wealthsimple">WealthSimple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_K._Johnson" title="Donald K. Johnson">Donald K. Johnson</a> Advisory Board, <a href="/wiki/BMO_Capital_Markets" title="BMO Capital Markets">BMO Capital Markets</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_A._Cope" title="George A. Cope">George Cope</a>, President, CEO, BCE Inc., <a href="/wiki/Bell_Canada" title="Bell Canada">Bell Canada</a>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible mw-made-collapsible" style="max-width: 100%">
<caption class="nowrap">Coat of arms of University of Western Ontario
<button type="button" class="mw-collapsible-toggle mw-collapsible-toggle-default" aria-expanded="true" tabindex="0"><span class="mw-collapsible-text">hide</span></button></caption>
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 220px;"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:UWOarms2014.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/UWOarms2014.jpg/250px-UWOarms2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="268" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/89/UWOarms2014.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="305" data-file-height="327"></a></span>
</td>
<td style="min-width:175px;">
<dl><dt>Notes</dt>
<dd>Granted by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Heraldic_Authority" title="Canadian Heraldic Authority">Canadian Heraldic Authority</a> on 15 January 2014<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></dd>
<dt>Crest</dt>
<dd>In front of a branch of maple Gules an open book proper edged and clasped Or.</dd>
<dt>Escutcheon</dt>
<dd>Per saltire Purpure and Argent in chief an open book proper edged and clasped Or in fess two hurts that to the dexter charged with a demi-stag contourn Argent that to the sinister charged with a demi-lion double-queued Ermine ducally crowned and in base a maple leaf, on a chief Or a sun rising Gules.</dd>
<dt>Supporters</dt>
<dd>Dexter a moose and sinister a lynx, both Or.</dd>
<dt>Motto</dt>
<dd><i>Veritas et Utilitas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for 'Truth and usefulness')</dd></dl>
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Western_Ontario&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239543626">.mw-parser-output .reflist{margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}@media screen{.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%}}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references" data-mw-group="lower-alpha">
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The university's main campus is located on 1151 Richmond Street in London, Ontario. However, in addition to its main campus the university also operates other facilities throughout southwestern Ontario.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The following includes full-time, and part-time students enrolled at the university. The following figures do not include students enrolled with an affiliate institutions of Western, including Brescia, King, and Huron university colleges.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106" aria-label="Jump up" title="Jump up">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The following includes students enrolled in a <a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="First professional degree">first professional degree</a> program.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
